		('Concrete individuals have a relation to time or space (they are in time and space).', 'http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#subClassOf', "Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. 		("Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.", '0', 'http://www.onto-med.de/ontologies/gfo.owl#Extrinsic_change')

		("Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.", '0', 'The instantiation relation holds between a category and an item. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. 		("Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.", 'http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#subClassOf', 'http://www.onto-med.de/ontologies/gfo.owl#Stratum')

		('AYn34JLrtD83xHb7JhkwVw==', '0', "Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.")

		('According to (Poli, 2001, 2002)  (based \non the philosopher Hartmann) we distinguish at least three ontological\nstrata of the world: the material stratum, the\nmental/psychological stratum, and the\nsocial stratum stratum. \n\nEvery entity of the world participates in certain\nstrata and levels. We take the position that the layers are\ncharacterized by integrated systems of categories. Hence, a layer can\nbe understood as a meta-category whose instances are categories of\ncertain kinds. Among these levels specific forms of categorial and\nexistential dependencies hold. For example, a mental entity requires\nan animate material object as its existential bearer.@en', 'http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#intersectionOf', 'bfR4eOJZyXjPBJB8fQaWkw==')

		('79968f91-4262-49ff-ab71-93dc35ad8421', '0', "Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.")

More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.")

		("Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.", 'http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#subClassOf', '0')

		('http://www.onto-med.de/ontologies/gfo.owl#Mass_entity', 'http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#subClassOf', "Property values usually appear in groups which are called value structures, value spaces or measurement systems.\nEach of these structures corresponds to some property. More intuitively, one could say that the property may be measured with respect to some measurement system.\nFor instance, sizes may be measured with the values ``small'' ``big'' or ``very big'', which are the elements of one value structure.\n\nThe notion of a value structure of a property is similar to a quality dimension in (Gardenfors, 2000).\n\nFurther, value structures are related to quality spaces in DOLCE (Masolo, 2003}. A quality space consists of all ``quales'' (our property values) of some ``quality'' (our property).\n\nOften it seems to be the case that a notion of distance can be defined, and that certain layers of value structures are isomorphic to some subset of real numbers, which allows for a mapping of values to pairs of a real number and a unit, as in the case of ``10 kg''.")
